Topic: Math
Context: Jennifer bought a box of Crunchy Grain cereal. The nutrition facts on the box state that a serving size of the cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories, 50 of which are calories from fat. In addition, each serving of the cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
Question: On Tuesday, Jennifer will mix Crunchy Grain cereal with Super Grain cereal for her breakfast. Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories per cup. If the total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270, how much Super Grain cereal is in one cup of the mixture?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{1}{8} \operatorname{cup}$
  B: $\frac{1}{4} \operatorname{cup}$
  C: $\frac{1}{3} \operatorname{cup}$
  D: $\frac{1}{2} \operatorname{cup}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A serving size of Crunchy Grain cereal is $\frac{3}{4}$ cup and provides 210 calories.
  Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 50 calories from fat.
  Each serving of Crunchy Grain cereal provides 180 milligrams of potassium, which is $5 \%$ of the daily allowance for adults.
  One cup of Super Grain cereal provides 240 calories.
  The total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is 270.
  
Action: 
Let's assume that Jennifer mixes $x$ cups of Super Grain cereal with $\frac{3}{4}-x$ cups of Crunchy Grain cereal.
The total number of calories in one cup of Jennifer's mixture is the sum of the number of calories in one cup of Super Grain cereal and the number of calories in one cup of Crunchy Grain cereal. 
We can write the following equation to solve for $x$:
$240x+ \frac{210}{\frac{3}{4}}(\frac{3}{4}-x)=270$
Simplifying the equation, we get:
$240x+280-210x=270$
$30x=270-280=-10$
$x=-\frac{10}{30}=-\frac{1}{3}$
Since $x$ represents the number of cups of Super Grain cereal, which must be positive, we can conclude that Jennifer mixes $\frac{1}{3}-\frac{3}{4}=-\frac{5}{12}$ cups of Super Grain cereal with $\frac{3}{4}$ cups of Crunchy Grain cereal. This is not a valid solution, so we must have made a mistake in our calculations.
Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$The equation above gives the height $h$, in feet, of a ball $t$ seconds after it is thrown straight up with an initial speed of $v$ feet per second from a height of $k$ feet. Which of the following gives $v$ in terms of $h, t$, and $k$ ?
Choices:
  A: $v=h+k-16 t$
  B: $v=\frac{h-k+16}{t}$
  C: $v=\frac{h+k}{t}-16 t$
  D: $v=\frac{h-k}{t}+16 t$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The given equation is a quadratic equation of the form $h = at^2 + bt + c$, where $a = -16$, $b = v$, and $c = k$.
  To find the initial velocity $v$, we need to use the formula for the derivative of a quadratic function: $f'(x) = 2ax + b$.
  In this case, $f(t) = h$, so $f'(t) = v$.
Action: 
  Taking the derivative of the given equation with respect to $t$, we get:
  $h' = 2at + b$
  Since $h' = v$, we have:
  $v = 2at + b$
  Substituting $a = -16$, $b = v$, and $c = k$, we get:
  $v = -32t + v$
  $v - v = -32t$
  $0 = -32t$
  $t = 0$
  This is not a valid solution, since the ball is thrown at time $t = 0$, so we cannot use this equation to find $v$ in terms of $h$, $t$, and $k$.
  Therefore, none of the given choices are correct. Answer("None of the Above")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The given equation is a quadratic equation in standard form, where $h$ is the height of the ball at time $t$, $v$ is the initial velocity of the ball, $k$ is the initial height of the ball, and $16$ is a constant that represents the acceleration due to gravity in feet per second squared.
  To solve for $v$, we need to isolate the term that contains $v$ on one side of the equation and simplify the remaining terms on the other side of the equation.
Action: 
  We can isolate the term that contains $v$ by rearranging the given equation as follows:
  $$h=k+v t-16 t^{2}$$
  Next, we can solve for $v$ by adding $16t^2$ to both sides of the equation and then dividing both sides by $t$:
  $$\begin{aligned} h+k&=v t+16 t^{2}\\ h+k+16 t^{2}&=v t\\ v&=\frac{h+k+16 t^{2}}{t} \end{aligned}$$
  Therefore, the answer is (C) $v=\frac{h+k}{t}+16 t$.
Response 2:
Knowledge:
The given equation is a quadratic equation in $t$.
When the ball reaches its maximum height, the velocity of the ball is zero.
At the maximum height, $h$ is the height of the ball, and $v$ is the velocity of the ball.
When the ball is thrown up, the initial velocity is $v$.
When the ball is at height $k$, the velocity of the ball is $v$.

We can find the maximum height of the ball by finding the vertex of the quadratic equation. The $t$-coordinate of the vertex is $-\frac{b}{2a}=\frac{-v}{2(-16)}=\frac{v}{32}$. Since the ball reaches its maximum height at the vertex, we have $h=k-\frac{v^{2}}{32}$.

Solving the equation for $v$, we have $v=\pm 4\sqrt{-2h+32k}$.

Since the ball is thrown up, $v$ is positive, so we have $v=4\sqrt{-2h+32k}$.

We can substitute this expression for $v$ into each of the answer choices to see which one is equivalent to the expression.

A: $h+k-16t=h+k-16t$
B: $\frac{h-k+16}{t}\neq 4\sqrt{-2h+32k}$
C: $\frac{h+k}{t}-16t\neq 4\sqrt{-2h+32k}$
D: $\frac{h-k}{t}+16t\neq 4\sqrt{-2h+32k}$

Therefore, the answer is None of the Above.

Response 4:
Knowledge:
The given equation is a quadratic equation in $t$ with a leading coefficient of $-16$. The coefficient of $t^2$ is negative which means the parabola opens downwards. The initial velocity is $v$ and the initial height is $k$.

Action: 
Solving the given equation for $v$, we get:
$$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$
$$h-k=-16 t^{2}+v t$$
$$v t=-16 t^{2}+h-k$$
$$v=\frac{-16 t^{2}+h-k}{t}$$
$$v=\frac{h-k}{t}-16t$$

$$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$

Solution:

$$h=-16 t^{2}+v t+k$$
$$h-k=-16 t^{2}+v t$$
$$v t=h-k+16 t^{2}$$
$$v=\frac{h-k+16 t^{2}}{t}$$

Question: $$-2 x+3 y=6$$In the $x y$-plane, the graph of which of the following equations is perpendicular to the graph of the equation above?
Choices:
  A: $3 x+2 y=6$
  B: $3 x+4 y=6$
  C: $2 x+4 y=6$
  D: $2 x+6 y=3$
Response 0:

  Two lines are perpendicular if and only if the product of their slopes is -1.
  The slope of a line in the form of $ax+by=c$ is $-\frac{a}{b}$.
  The given equation can be rewritten as $y=\frac{2}{3}x+2$.
  A: The slope of the line $3x+2y=6$ is $-\frac{3}{2}$.
  B: The slope of the line $3x+4y=6$ is $-\frac{3}{4}$.
  C: The slope of the line $2x+4y=6$ is $-\frac{1}{2}$.
  D: The slope of the line $2x+6y=3$ is $-\frac{1}{3}$.
Action: Answer("B")  
The slope of the line $3x+4y=6$ is $-\frac{3}{4}$, and $\frac{-2}{3} \cdot \frac{-4}{3} = 1$, so the graph of $3x+4y=6$ is perpendicular to the graph of $-2x+3y=6$.

### Exam: sat-math-100 | Temperature: 2.0 | Problem 99 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: $$\begin{aligned}& k x-3 y=4 \\& 4 x-5 y=7\end{aligned}$$In the system of equations above, $k$ is a constant and $x$ and $y$ are variables. For what value of $k$ will the system of equations have no solution?
Choices:
  A: $\frac{12}{5}$
  B: $\frac{16}{7}$
  C: $-\frac{16}{7}$
  D: $-\frac{12}{5}$
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  For a system of linear equations to have no solution, the lines must be parallel, which means they have the same slope and different y-intercepts.
  The slope of the first equation is $k/3$, and the slope of the second equation is $4/5$.
  The two lines will be parallel if $k/3 = 4/5$ and the y-intercepts are different.
  The y-intercept of the first equation is $(0, -4/3)$, and the y-intercept of the second equation is $(0, 7/5)$.
  The y-intercepts are different if $-4/3 \neq 7/5$.
Action: 
  Solving $k/3 = 4/5$ for $k$, we get $k = \frac{12}{5} \cdot \frac{1}{3} = \frac{4}{5}$.
  Since $-4/3 \neq 7/5$, we know that the lines will be parallel for $k = \boxed{\textbf{(A) }\frac{12}{5}}$.
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  We can use the determinant of the coefficient matrix to determine whether the system of equations has a unique solution, no solution, or infinitely many solutions. If the determinant is zero, then the system has either no solution or infinitely many solutions. 
  The determinant of the coefficient matrix is $k(-5)-(-3)(4)=-5k+12$.
  If $-5k+12=0$, then the determinant is zero and the system has either no solution or infinitely many solutions.
Action: 
  Solve $-5k+12=0$ to get $k=\frac{12}{5}$. 
  Therefore, if $k=\frac{12}{5}$, then the system of equations will have no solution. 
  Answer: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  We can use the determinant of the coefficient matrix to determine if a system of linear equations has a unique solution, no solution, or infinitely many solutions. If the determinant is zero, then the system has either no solution or infinitely many solutions. If the determinant is nonzero, then the system has a unique solution.
